Reply from the Shanghai Shipping Industry Association: Respectfully, we have received your two letters of September 29th and October 13th, and we have listened to them carefully. Upon investigation, regarding the refusal of China Merchants, Sanbei, and Chang'an to load Fujian goods, we have sent separate letters to inquire after receiving the first letter. We have not received a reply yet. We have continued to urge a reply after receiving the second letter. Once we receive a reply, we will report it immediately. We are replying by letter first. This is addressed to the Jiangxi Minbei Merchants Association stationed in Shanghai, from Yu Qiaqing, Chairman of the Shanghai Shipping Industry Association.

Document submitted to the Navigation Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications and the Social Affairs Bureau of the Shanghai Municipal Government: Submitted for the Shanghai domestic shipping companies violating transportation conventions, refusing to load goods from the Jiangxi gang to Fujian, resulting in huge losses, please immediately ban them according to law and quickly order them to load and transport as usual. Upon investigation, shipping transport is a public transportation business. The transport of passengers and goods should be treated equally unless there are special circumstances such as full capacity, excessive goods, or outstanding freight charges. There should be no acceptance of this and rejection of that. However, the Shanghai China Merchants, Sanbei, and Chang'an shipping companies suddenly refused to load the yarn and other goods sold by Jiangxi merchants stationed in Shanghai to Northern Fujian in mid-September, causing the cargo transport to be interrupted and the losses to be unrecoverable. The reason for the refusal was not clearly stated, and there was no reply to repeated inquiries. We sent a letter to the Shanghai Shipping Industry Association, ordering the companies to transport as usual, but they ignored it for a long time. Such independent shipping, refusing to transport goods, not only hinders transportation and damages commerce, but also violates the Three Principles of the People and industrial policy. The China Merchants Bureau has been nationalized and should not take the same steps as private enterprises. Other privately owned companies should also be supervised by the competent authorities in accordance with Article 3 of the Regulations on the Supervision of Private Public Utility Enterprises. If there is any obstruction of public transport or damage to social security, the situation should be dealt with in accordance with Article 10 of the same regulations. According to the first paragraph of Article 154 of the Civil Code, once a shipping company schedules a voyage, it is an expression of an offer and should be binding, and it has no power to refuse any merchant's consignment of goods. It is said that the companies are refusing to load the goods of the Jiangxi merchants due to the illegal donation movement of the Fujian merchants, which is not only obviously unfair, but also legally impermissible. For this reason, we petition your bureau to approve the ban and order the China Merchants, Sanbei, and Chang'an shipping companies to load and transport the goods of Jiangxi merchants stationed in Shanghai as usual in order to facilitate transportation and maintain commerce, and we are eagerly awaiting orders. We respectfully submit this to the Navigation Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications and the Social Affairs Bureau of the Shanghai Municipal Government.

Approval from the Navigation Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications: We have received the submission and have separately instructed the China Merchants Bureau and the Sanbei and Chang'an shipping companies to investigate and reply. We should wait for the reply before reviewing it. Please be informed. This approval is given by Zhu Yaoting, Director of the Bureau.

Rejecting Private 164

Participation, discriminating against the people, is really not as good as taking away from them. According to which principles is this justified? In countries around the world, railways and ships are divided into state-owned and private. State-owned roads are more numerous than private roads, and private ships are more numerous than state-owned ships. However, for water-land joint transport, both the road and shipping companies are freely combined. Governments have no precedent of monopolizing it, no special permission for state-owned companies to take precedence, and no restrictions on abandoning private companies. Therefore, the circulation of goods is increasing day by day, and transportation is becoming increasingly developed. Advanced models should be followed. Moreover, facts speak louder than words and are generally recognized by the world. The same is true for joint transport. Ships are the tools of joint transport and should be used widely. The Shanghai-Qingdao line, the Shanghai-Haizhou line, and the lines starting from Changsha are all connected to the railway and are important focuses of joint transport. However, the China Merchants Bureau does not have suitable ships to operate. If they want to monopolize joint transport, the obstruction of goods will be inevitable. Once goods are obstructed, industry and commerce will suffer, and the railway will be affected as well. When they realize they have been fooled, it will be too late to regret their miscalculation. These are all facts that cannot be concealed. Therefore,

For the Sake of the Railway 165

The ships for joint transport must be widespread and numerous, so that contacts can be made quickly and things can be transported back and forth without interruption. There will be no long-term accumulation of goods in warehouses, the transportation will be properly distributed, and the supply and demand of vehicles will be easier to adjust. Passengers and goods can be transported at any time, so merchants will find it more convenient to trade, and the increase in railway revenue can be guaranteed. Otherwise, it is not a policy that benefits both oneself and others. Most of the goods transported by domestic ships come from the railway or go to the railway. Therefore, although the combination of water and land transport is nominally called a combination, it is actually a joint venture. In other words, the goods transported by the railway are the source of the ship's water freight. It is no different from the source of livelihood of private shipping enterprises. In recent years, the gradual increase in private ships and the prolongation of the lifeline of private shipping have all depended on this. Now, the joint military affairs are eliminating private shipping enterprises, which is simply cutting off their source of livelihood and putting them to death. Since the rise of the revolutionary army, private ships have provided more military supplies than the China Merchants Bureau. The government also pays rent to the ships of the China Merchants Bureau according to the example of private shipping ships. Therefore, China Merchants has not only failed to fully fulfill its obligations to the country, but also sometimes evaded and reluctantly fulfilled them.

The Facts Are All There 166

Check and verify, the obligation and the right come into being by nature, and should be implemented relatively. Now, in military affairs that are detrimental to business, private companies are ordered to bear more obligations, while in joint transport that is related to life and death, private companies are not allowed to enjoy the same rights. Is this fair in terms of reason and logic? Moreover, the bird has not been completely exhausted, but the dog has already been cooked. Since the treatment is different, it is inevitable to wait and see. At a time when military affairs have not yet been completed, the impact is particularly profound. Moreover, according to the organization of water-land joint transport, it is actually a contribution to the recovery of shipping rights. Shipping merchants deeply sympathize. However, this matter is of great importance and should gather the entire force in order to achieve the effect of the same heart and the same virtue. Since the shipping merchants have repeatedly called for it, the Ministry of Railways has already expressed that "it will gradually need to be promoted in the future, and private shipping companies can be considered for membership based on the transportation situation." This shows that the original proposal to allow only state-owned enterprises to operate has been changed. However, because it is difficult to change suddenly, the future promotion is used as a reservation. However, shipping merchants believe that although there are verbal promises, there is no fixed date, and it will become a bubble when time passes. Moreover, everything should be planned from the beginning, and decisions should be made immediately. Since they are allowed to join, they should start cooperating to show great fairness and to achieve long-term peace. We should ask the association to telegraph to the Central Party Department of the National Government and the Executive Yuan to grant relief, order the Ministry of Railways to allow private shipping enterprises to undertake water-land joint transport at the same time as state-owned enterprises, not to distinguish between the order of time, to treat them equally, not to use the empty words of promotion, to immediately implement benefits. Otherwise, private shipping enterprises will have their source of livelihood cut off and have no way to survive on their own. The situation is urgent, and they have no choice but to close their business together in order to fulfill the plans of those who abandoned the people. Furthermore, at a time when military affairs have not been completed, private shipping enterprises and military transport are very closely related, and we also ask the association to telegraph to the Military Commission, responsible for overlooking the situation and providing assistance, so that we can carry out reconstruction and save the dying. The association replied that the provisions of the Provisional Constitution and principles, facts and reasonings, are all real, and their state of panic and fear has been witnessed by the association. Moreover, their request, which is in line with what the Ministry of Railways has already promised, differs only in one thing. If they are allowed to handle it at the same time to comfort them, it does not seem to be a very difficult matter. Since everyone is in agreement, we will deliver it on your behalf. We sincerely ask you to examine and approve it and order it to be implemented, so as to maintain the people's hearts and protect private shipping. We are extremely anxious and await orders. Yu Hede and others of the Shanghai Shipping Industry Association respectfully kowtow.

Swire: The Xiamen Workers' Strike Did Not Materialize. The Strike Was Halted After Persuasion by the Xiamen Authorities. 168

The Swire Company's Xiamen dockworkers, in order to support the workers in the middle hold of the Wusong steamer and respond to the strike in Guangdong, have recently affected the cargo transported by the company's Nan Hua vessels from Shanghai to Xiamen and Shantou. Yesterday, the company received a telegram from Xiamen reporting that there was no strike. Details are as follows:

No Strike in Xiamen 169

The Xiamen Swire Company dockworkers were originally scheduled to start ceasing loading and unloading work today, causing many Hakka merchants in Shanghai to dare not declare their goods for loading. Yesterday at 1 p.m., the Shanghai branch received an urgent telegram from the Xiamen branch reporting that the strike had been effectively banned by the local government. The original telegram stated, "The Xiamen authorities have informed the Seamen's Association not to strike and have ordered the Association to notify the various ports that Xiamen will definitely not have a strike," etc. Yesterday, the company translated the telegram and informed the local Xiamen Hakka merchants to load goods as usual.

No News from Shantou 170

Initially, it was widely rumored that Shantou would also take the same action as Xiamen and implement a strike, but it would depend on the action of Xiamen. Now that Xiamen has been banned by the authorities and persuaded to end the strike, Shantou should also have no problem. However, as of last night, there was no telegram from Shantou. Today, the Swire Nan Hua vessels will operate as usual between Shanghai and Shantou and will carry passengers and goods.

Transportation Affected 171

In the past four or five days, after the news of the Xiamen-Shantou strike spread, the Hakka merchants of Xiamen and Shantou in Shanghai, fearing that their scattered goods would be obstructed, temporarily returned them, causing the Swire Company to suffer losses in its export business. Now that the telegram has proven that large quantities of goods and transit goods can be loaded as usual, the company will send the telegram to the branch offices in various ports to continue collecting and transporting Xiamen and Shantou goods.

Municipal Authorities Actively Planning Greater Shanghai Transportation 172

The areas of Huinan and Zhabei in this city are seeing visible prosperity. Recently, in order to promote the Greater Shanghai Plan, the municipal government will first develop the downtown area. However, transportation is crucial to the prosperity of the city. Therefore, the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities is actively planning transportation in the Chinese-administered areas. Here are the details we have learned:

Huinan Area 173

Although there are currently trams running, operating trams is too expensive and takes too long. In fact, it will be difficult to expand them in the short term. Recently, the Huashang Tram Company has a plan to build another line from Huinan to the new western district, but this project is heavy and cannot be realized in one or two years. In the past, public buses operated in Huinan, which was very convenient for the city. However, due to the impact of the January 28th Incident, it was announced that they would be closed. However, the poor management of the Huinan public buses was also a major reason for the company's closure. Therefore, recently, the municipal government has decided to operate public buses in Huinan on its own. The route will first be tried out on the same route that the Huinan Public Bus Company used to operate. If it is successful, it will be expanded. The plan is currently being carefully discussed by the Bureau of Public Utilities, the Bureau of Finance, and other bureaus.

Zhabei Area 174

In the future, the company will take the downtown area as the transportation center of Northern Shanghai. In addition to running from Zhabei to the downtown area, it will also extend north to Wusong and east to Yangshupu. The company has already ordered 12 public buses or 3.5-ton big Montian chassis from the United States, which have already arrived at the port. The bodies are being built, and all routes will be tested after being approved by the Municipal Bureau of Public Utilities.

Former Secretary of the Ministry of Railways Accused of Embezzling Public Bonds – Arrested on Great Western Road – Transferred from the Special Court to the Local Court 175

Hu Tianjun, a native of Anhui, 40 years old, residing at No. 14 Anle Lane, Jing'an Temple Road, served as the Chief Accountant of the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Railways in 1931. Subsequently, the office was ordered to be abolished, and Hu was transferred to the position of Secretary of the Ministry of Railways. He resigned in January of this year and came to Shanghai to engage in commerce, partnering with others to open the Daxia Automobile Company at No. 271 Great Western Road in western Shanghai, with Hu serving as the manager. Recently, the Ministry of Railways suspected that Hu had embezzled public bonds worth $3,500 during his tenure as Chief Accountant and secretly ordered the Shanghai Local Court Prosecutor's Office to investigate and arrest him. As Hu resided in the Public Concession, the court prepared documents and dispatched court police Xu Guoguang and Gu Hanqing to report to the First Special District Court in the afternoon the day before, requesting assistance. The court approved the request, issued an arrest warrant, and sent it to the Jing'an Temple Road Police Station, which, together with Chinese detective Liu Zheng Gang and Western detective Lawley, went to the Daxia Automobile Company, arrested Hu Tianjun, and brought him to the police station. Yesterday morning, he was escorted to the Eighth Criminal Division of the First Special District Court, where court police Gu Hanqing filed the case, explaining the previous situation and requesting permission for transfer. Subsequently, police station lawyer Wang Yaotang stated that he had no objection to the transfer but requested to review the official documents from the Prosecutor's Office. Hu Tianjun stated that he served as the Chief Accountant of the Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Railways in 1931 and that all public bonds were kept under his seal. Later, the office was ordered to close, and he was reassigned as Secretary. He then handed over his duties and discovered that 3,500 yuan of public bonds were missing. He reported this to the person in charge of the ministry and expressed his willingness to bear the responsibility for compensation, but this has not been fulfilled to date. He also retained lawyers Da Yaoxian and Wei Wenhan to appear in court to defend him and oppose the transfer, stating that based on Hu's statements, the matter seemed to be of a civil nature, not involving criminal matters, and that his place of business was also located in the Public Concession, which the court had jurisdiction over. Even if Hu had indeed committed embezzlement, it would fall under the amnesty ordinance, and the crime he deserved would have been extinguished. Based on these three points, they requested the court to accept the case and allow Hu to be released on bail. Judge Xue Lanru reviewed the report and ordered that Hu Tianjun be allowed to be taken back by the officials from the Local Court Prosecutor's Office for interrogation. Hu's lawyers, upon hearing the order, immediately stated that they would file an appeal against this decision. The court granted the appeal.

Japanese Thief Disguised as Chinese Arrested in the Red Light District – Broke into Dentist's Office – Robbed 600 Yuan in Cash 176

Yesterday, the Shanghai Daily reported that Yoshikawa Kanezo (32 years old), who carried a weapon and broke into the Zhang Dental Clinic on Zhejiang Road in May of this year, robbing 600 yuan in cash, has since disappeared and lived in hiding in the French Concession. Abbot of Guoen Temple Plots to Imprison Junior Monk – Evil Plan Arose from Desire for Power – False Accusations Deceived Wang Yiting – Monk Kaijue Imprisoned in Xiqin Institute – Truth Revealed, Brother Files Grievance 177

Guoen Temple on Rue de Virieu in the French Concession and Chaoyin Cave Temple on Putuo Mountain in Ningbo are both affiliated temples of the Zizhulin Temple on Putuo Mountain. The Abbot of Guoen Temple, Kaisheng, and the Abbot of Chaoyin Cave Temple, Kaijue, both became monks at Zizhulin. In terms of lineage, they are distant brothers. Kaijue is a disciple of Zhizheng, the Abbot of Zizhulin, while Kaisheng is Zhizheng's nephew. According to the regulations of Zizhulin, the abbots of Guoen Temple and Chaoyin Cave Temple must be replaced every three years, appointed by the Abbot. However, Kaisheng has been the Abbot of Guoen Temple for over ten years, possessing tens of thousands in temple property and addicted to opium. He also has a very adventurous nature. After the death of Zhizheng, the Abbot of Zizhulin, two years ago, Kaijue came to Shanghai to meet with Kaisheng and requested to switch positions between Guoen Temple and Chaoyin Cave Temple. Kaisheng did not express his opinion at the time. Soon after, Kaijue returned to the mountain, but Kaisheng actually suspected that Kaijue wanted to seize his position as Abbot of Guoen Temple. According to the regulations, he could not disobey, so he became jealous of Kaijue and hatched an evil plan to expel Kaijue. By removing Kaijue, he could personally obtain the lucrative positions of Abbot of both temples and wield all the power. Therefore, he plotted to remove Kaijue by fabricating various accusations against him and falsely informing Wang Yiting, a lay Buddhist in Shanghai, asking Wang to write a letter sending Kaijue to the Caohejing Xiqin Institute for vagrants (founded by the Shanghai Charity Organization, with Wang as the chairman), restricting his freedom. He could then safely take over the position of Abbot of Chaoyin Cave Temple. Wang did not discern the truth and readily agreed, first writing a letter to the Xiqin Institute, instructing them to receive and detain Kaijue when he was sent by Guoen Temple. Kaisheng, having made arrangements, waited for Kaijue to come to Shanghai and fall into his trap. In August of last year, when Kaijue came to Shanghai from Putuo Mountain to collect donations, he went to Guoen Temple to meet with Kaisheng. At that time, Kaisheng falsely told Kaijue, "I have a grand-disciple, Yuanlin, who is very bad, smokes opium, and commits various illegal acts, violating the precepts. I plan to send him to the Caohejing Xiqin Institute for vagrants to help him quit smoking. I have already contacted the institute and they have agreed. Because I myself am addicted, it is inconvenient for me to send him myself. Please accompany Yuanlin to the institute for me," etc. At that time, Kaijue was completely unaware of the plot and thought it was a good deed to send a grand-disciple to quit smoking, so he rashly agreed and accompanied Yuanlin to the Xiqin Institute for vagrants, where he was detained along with Yuanlin and not allowed to return. After arguing with the staff, he was told that Wang Yiting had written a letter from Guoen Temple instructing them to receive and detain both of them. At this point, Kaijue was helpless and had no choice but to submit. However, when Kaijue came to Shanghai from Putuo, he entrusted the position of Abbot of Chaoyin Cave Temple to a guest monk friend, Shuhua, for a month. When Shuhua did not see Kaijue return to the mountain after the deadline, he became suspicious. At this time, Kaisheng went to Chaoyin Cave Temple on Putuo Mountain to take over the position of Abbot and told the guest monks and others in the temple that Kaijue had committed a crime in Shanghai, was facing legal trouble, and had already died. Shuhua did not believe him and refused to allow Kaisheng to take over the position, and came to Shanghai to search for Kaijue. After spending months, he had no news until recently when he learned that Kaijue had been imprisoned by Kaisheng in the Xiqin Institute for vagrants. He was shocked and returned to Putuo, informing Kaijue's brother, Monk Jing'an, who came to Shanghai and went to the Xiqin Institute to meet with Kaijue. After learning the whole story, he contacted Kaisheng, but to no avail. Therefore, Jing'an hired lawyers Li Mian and Chen Qun to file a criminal self-accusation with the Second Special District Court, accusing Kaisheng of obstructing freedom and requesting that the case be investigated. The court accepted the case and summoned the parties yesterday afternoon. Kaijue was detained, so his brother Jing'an and lawyer Li appeared in court. The defendant claimed illness and sent lawyers Yuan Xitao and others to appear on his behalf. At 3 p.m., Judge Li Changnian heard the case in the Second Criminal Division. First, the plaintiff's representative, Jing'an, stated that Kaijue and Kaisheng were both abbots and described how Kaijue was imprisoned by Kaisheng, requesting that the defendant be strictly summoned to court for questioning and that Kaijue be brought to court for release and restoration of freedom. Next, the defendant's lawyer stated that the defendant was suffering from hemoptysis and was being treated at the Guanghua Hospital in Ningbo. He had received a letter saying that his condition was serious and requested a postponement for him to appear in court for questioning. Finally, Monk Shuhua testified. The court ordered a postponement to November 18th at 2 p.m., instructing the defendant to appear in court and requesting the Xiqin Institute for vagrants to send Kaijue to court for questioning.

Lawyer Tian Heming Sues Doctor Yu Songyun – Malpractice Causes Postpartum Woman to Contract Dysentery – Young Woman Gu Linyi Dies of Diarrhea After Childbirth 178

According to the Xin Xin News Agency, Tian Heming, a Doctor of Law from the United States, who has a law firm at No. 170 Jiangxi Road, his wife Ms. Gu Linyi (a graduate of Shanghai Law and Politics College) previously gave birth at the Sino-German Obstetrics Hospital at No. 282 Lane, Jing'an Temple Road. Dr. Yu Songyun, the director of the hospital, because the postpartum woman had difficulty defecating, used a leather enema. Also, because the postpartum woman's breasts were swollen, he used ice packs on her breasts, causing Tian's wife Gu to develop diarrhea and eventually die. Tian believes that his wife's death was due to Dr. Yu's malpractice. Yesterday, he filed a special petition with the Shanghai First Special District Court, bringing a criminal self-accusation against Yu for killing through medical negligence. The original petition is excerpted as follows:

Ice Packs on Breasts Cause Postpartum Woman's Death 179

Requesting a severe punishment for killing through medical negligence. My wife, Ms. Gu Linyi, a graduate of Shanghai Law and Politics College, entered the Sino-German Obstetrics Hospital (located at No. 282 Lane, Jing'an Temple Road) set up by the defendant at 8 a.m. on July 29th to await childbirth. The defendant, together with midwife Qiu Lizhen, delivered the baby. She gave birth at 1:34 a.m. that night (i.e., 1:34 a.m. on July 30th the next day). Afterwards, at around 11 a.m. on August 2nd, the defendant, because the postpartum woman had difficulty defecating, used a leather enema. The next day, at around 11 a.m. on August 3rd, the defendant, because the postpartum woman's breasts were swollen, used ice packs on her breasts, starting from 11 a.m. that day until 3 a.m. on August 4th the next day. At this time, the postpartum woman suddenly felt diarrhea, and only then did they stop using the ice packs (from 9:30 p.m. on August 3rd to 3 a.m. on August 4th the next day, the postpartum woman was asleep, but the ice packs continued to be placed on her breasts). My wife was healthy before childbirth, and also healthy after childbirth before the onset of diarrhea at 3 a.m. on August 4th. The defendant also called it a healthy delivery. Now, suddenly, after six days and five hours since entering the hospital, i.e., five days and one and a half hours after childbirth, she started having diarrhea, which feels quite bizarre. According to obstetrical experience, if a postpartum woman has a disease, it should occur within three days after childbirth. If there is no disease within three days, then the dangerous period for the postpartum woman has passed. In this case, my wife started having diarrhea on August 4th and continued until August 7th. Every day she had diarrhea fifty or seventy times or more. Her symptoms were thirst but no appetite, vomiting, colic, restlessness, insomnia, and the cessation of vaginal bleeding. The postpartum woman's symptoms were so severe and lasted for four or five days. The defendant failed to identify the deadly dysentery bacteria and failed to find the source of the disease, merely making empty promises and perfunctorily dealing with it. Because I saw the postpartum woman's condition worsening day by day, I moved her out of the defendant's hospital at 6 a.m. on August 8th in order to seek medical treatment from another doctor. At first, the defendant did not allow her to be discharged, and then forced me to sign a guarantee, stating that I would exempt the defendant from any responsibility. After the postpartum woman was discharged, she was sent to Tongde Hospital for treatment that afternoon. However, because her body was weak after childbirth, she should not have been attacked by any disease. Also, because the dysentery had lasted too long, her physical strength was completely exhausted. In addition, dysentery toxins spread throughout her body, and she eventually died on the afternoon of August 16th.

Reasons Listed to the Court 180

My wife's death was due to the defendant's malpractice. The reasons are listed below: (1) Postpartum women are most afraid of catching a cold. The defendant should not have allowed the postpartum woman to use ice packs while sleeping. The diarrhea occurred after the ice packs were applied, indicating that the ice packs caused the postpartum woman to catch a cold and reduced her resistance, which promoted the growth of dysentery bacteria. (2) Dysentery is an infectious disease and cannot occur without external bacteria entering the body. My wife was healthy after childbirth and only started having diarrhea after five days and one and a half hours. From a medical perspective, it is clear that it was caused by dysentery bacteria on the leather enema used on the morning of August 2nd entering her intestines. (The defendant's hospital has no disinfection equipment, and the enema is often inserted into the intestines of patients, so there are many bacteria attached). (3) The defendant used counterfeit medicine and reported a small amount as a large amount, deceiving the patient's family, which aggravated the disease, delayed treatment, and eventually led to the patient's death. (4) The postpartum woman had a high number of bowel movements when she first started having diarrhea on the morning of August 4th, indicating a severe condition. For several days from August 5th to August 7th, the defendant failed to identify the source of the disease and did not entrust others to check for dysentery bacteria, which clearly constitutes professional negligence. Based on the above facts and reasons, my wife was first infected with dysentery bacteria due to the defendant's negligence, then developed dysentery due to the defendant's negligence, and finally died due to the defendant's negligence and delay in treatment. From having no illness to becoming ill and then dying, it was all caused by the defendant. The defendant has violated the provisions of Article 27 and Article 291, paragraph 3 of the Criminal Law on the crime of homicide. Therefore, I specially request the court, in accordance with Article 338 of the Criminal Procedure Law, to severely punish the defendant according to law in order to uphold humanity and serve public convenience. Furthermore, because I have been inquiring about medical opinions from various sources, I have been delayed until now before filing the lawsuit. Also, I will submit another petition detailing the three items regarding this case: (A) detailed facts of the events, (B) medical basis, and (C) legal basis.

The most interesting new scene is the aerial performance, with the actors spinning in the air above the audience, which is truly a spectacle. In addition, there is a brand new bamboo pole equilibrium scene, with one male and one female actor each climbing to the top of a bamboo pole, while another actor on the ground uses his head and chest to support it, and the actors at the top perform various acrobatic feats in the air. This scene is very dangerous. The world's smallest and strongest "Baomi" will perform new feats of strength. "Tai Kuan" and his agile sea lions have new acts to entertain the audience. Hagenbeck and his well-trained horses, the female rider and her dancing horse, the giant elephant of "Batorai" and the Shetland ponies, the agile "Kala" brothers, the Indian elephants trained by "Walt," Hagenbeck's beautiful horses, and everything else are completely different from what was seen the first time. Ticket prices remain the same, from 60 cents for the cheapest seats to 5 yuan for the boxes. All seats from 1 yuan to 4 yuan are very comfortable and have excellent views. The zoo is open daily from 10 a.m. to 6 p.m. Admission is 50 cents for adults and 20 cents for children.

First Special Court Burns Confiscated Narcotics 192

The Shanghai First Special District Court, as per regulations, every three months, submits a report to the department for approval to publicly burn confiscated narcotics, such as opium, morphine, red pills, and heroin, etc., in order to emphasize the prohibition of opium and eliminate the poisonous atmosphere. Now, due to the large quantity of various narcotics accumulated in the recent three months, the court president, Mr. Guo Yunguan, in accordance with the usual practice, submitted a report to the Ministry of Justice and received approval to handle the matter according to established cases. The burning was scheduled for 2 PM yesterday, and the location was still the Yizhongdi (public cemetery) of the Bao'an Hall on the south side of the court. President Guo had previously invited representatives from various municipal Party, government, military, and police organizations, the Lawyers' Association, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and other groups, as well as the Municipal Council, to attend the site for supervision. Starting from 1 PM, court clerks were ordered to transport each item of narcotics to be burned from the evidence room to the burning site. Several prosecutors from the Higher Second Branch Procuratorate were dispatched to the site to assist with the supervision, along with investigators, prosecutors, and clerks from the First Special Court. The surrounding area of the burning site was closely guarded by bailiffs. Each type of narcotic was first unsealed and inspected by the supervising investigators and prosecutors to ensure the quality and quantity, with extraordinary attention paid to avoid any malpractices. After the narcotics were thrown into the fire, kerosene and salt were sprinkled to ensure that the ashes were also rendered useless before being thrown into the Huangpu River, effectively eradicating the root of the problem. Therefore, the work was extremely tedious, and the time spent was inevitably longer, until the twilight deepened before the matter was concluded.

Dyeing Industry Cloth Office Completed Organization Today, Declaration Issued Regarding Rejection of Dyed Goods 193

According to Xin Sheng She, the dyeing industry workers in this city, in order to demand the restoration of the original "wine money" agreement, have been on strike for ten days, and the issue remains unresolved. The industry union's cloth office, after being ordered by the Municipal Party Department to reorganize, has announced its completion and will hold a general meeting today. The office, due to this work stoppage, fears that various sectors do not understand the truth and has issued a declaration. The original text is as follows: This office's work stoppage is aimed at urging capital to restore the old agreement rights and separate the "wine money," which is the unanimous demand of all workers and staff. The request to restore the old agreement treatment, in terms of human sentiment, is the wage crystallized from the sweat and blood of each worker and staff member, which should provide for their livelihood. The capital side should show compassion for the laborers, promote mutual benefit, and uphold the principles of both law and reason. The aforementioned "wine money" old agreement was signed by the Municipal Government's Bureau of Agriculture, Industry, and Commerce before 1927, as a legal agreement. In other words, it is a specific guarantee contract for the "wine money" that laborers should receive. The capital side should sincerely fulfill it, but instead, they have neglected it for a long time, disregarding the livelihoods of the labor side. Workers and staff are starving and cold, which not only worries the workers themselves but also indirectly cuts off the livelihoods of families dependent on wages. Facing starvation, they have no choice but to make a final appeal. This work stoppage is a legitimate demand for the capital side to consider the lives of the workers and is a peaceful warning. It is not a conflict or impulse between labor and capital. The workers remain calm throughout the situation. The existence of "wine money" for dyeing workers dates back to the Tongzhi era. Cloth merchants urgently needed to sell dyed cloth, so they entrusted workers to rush the dyeing and delivery. The workers, working tirelessly without adequate rest, contributed to the rapid dyeing. As a result, cloth merchants were able to seize the opportunity to sell goods, and they paid workers "wine money," which is their wage, passed down through generations. It has become an agreement through custom, and the agreement has been guaranteed by government agencies. At the same time, the cloth merchants' staff also have "flower bubbles" (bonuses), which is similar to the payment of "wine money" to the workers, and the two do not conflict. It has become an established custom and necessary benefit. Now, because cloth merchants often do not follow the dyeing price agreement signed in 1927 and the agreed unit prices for various new products in 1930, they continuously deprive and reduce costs. The "wine money," which is included in the dyeing price, is drawn into the capital side's loss-making path and disappears, leaving the laborers unable to support themselves. Workers and staff are forced to take this action. The goals of the work stoppage are: (1) to restore the original agreement treatment, urging capital to implement the rights stipulated in the legally signed agreement, while also including a supplementary condition of "three masters and one apprentice"; (2) to separate the "wine money" to protect the workers' autonomy and eliminate future labor-capital disputes. Separating the "wine money," which is included in the dyeing price, from a fundamental perspective does not involve or affect anything. Furthermore, the Qinglan Industry Union has already set a precedent for separating "wine money," which can be used as a basis. This office's advocacy is purely for the restoration of legal contract rights and the liberation of workers from suffering, with firm determination and no turning back. Fearing that various sectors do not understand the truth, the facts and difficulties are fully explained, hoping that various public organizations and labor unions will provide sympathetic assistance to resolve the crisis. This is the declaration.

Drivers' Association Schedules Enlarged Meeting 194

The China Navigation Drivers' Association was founded by Guangji captain Xu Zhimin and others in February of this year. In June, a general meeting was held to establish the association, which was approved by the China Seamen's Special Party Department, the Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau, and the Central Party Department's People's Movement Committee. Child Unable to Speak Local Dialect, Difficult to Determine Parentage, Blood Test Needed to Verify Mother-Child Relationship, Abductors Detained Pending Further Interrogation 195

Wang Jinsheng, a Chinese detective from the Huishan Police Station, previously arrested Cantonese woman Li Huangshi, 19, and man Huang Lizan at the Huishan Wharf on the Yuansheng wheel for child abduction and recovered a three-year-old boy named Bingquan. Subsequently, at 227 Taishide Road, 27 Xujiahui Road, and other places in the French Concession, two more Cantonese women, Lin Lishi, and Taixing woman Zhou Zhushi, were apprehended and taken to the First Special District Court. Interrogation revealed that the child was brought to Shanghai by Zhou Zhushi from their hometown in June and was sold to Li Huangshi as a grandson for fifty yuan through Lin Lishi's introduction. Zhou Zhushi confessed that the child's real name was Deyi and that his father, Luo Tianzhang, worked as a helper in the Wanhualou restaurant in Dongmen, Taixing. Because the family was poor, they were willing to sell the child to others as a son, and the money was taken back by his father. Li Huangshi possessed a bill of sale for the child. The case was complex, and the three women were ordered to be detained. The Taixing County government was to be notified to investigate, and the child was to be sent to the Women and Children Relief Society for care. Huang Lizan was released on bail pending further notice. Yesterday morning, Judge Xiao Xiefen presided over a continued trial. After the police lawyer Zhang Tianyin recounted the events, Luo Wangshi, a woman from Taixing, claimed that the child was her youngest son. She had three sons in total. Her husband, Tianzhang, had a stall selling peanuts in Dongmen, their hometown. Because the family was poor, and she suffered from a sore on her right foot, leaving her with a limp, she could not care for the child. Therefore, she came to Shanghai with Zhou Zhushi in the summer to sell the child, receiving fifty yuan. Her remaining words were evasive, which contradicted Zhou Zhushi's previous testimony and suggested collusion in the abduction. However, because the child was young and unable to speak, it was questionable whether he was Luo Wangshi's son. When questioned, Li Huangshi stated that the child was brought by Lin Lishi and Zhou Zhushi, and his mother, Luo Wangshi, was not present at the time. Lin Wangshi testified that she knew Li Huangshi and Zhou Zhushi but only acted as a go-between and received no benefit. Zhou Zhushi's testimony was ambiguous. The court examined the bill of sale, which stated that the child was the son of the Zhang family, not the Luo family, and was signed by Zhou Zhushi. Therefore, the judge could not determine whether Luo Wangshi was the child's mother. It was ruled that they would be temporarily detained, and a blood test would be conducted to verify the mother-child relationship. Li, Lin, and Zhou were detained, while Huang Lizan remained on bail pending further verification.

Yihe Rubber Factory Labor Dispute Resolved 196

The labor dispute at the Yihe Rubber Factory on South Minzhe Road in Shanghai was mediated by the Rubber Workers' Union of the First District, but the mediation failed. Xu Jianzhu, Cheng Dong, and Zhao Maolin were then recommended to appeal to the Party and government for relief. Zhao Erchang from the Municipal Party Department and Lin Damo from the Social Bureau were dispatched to the factory to conduct mediation. As a result of the negotiations, it was agreed that the back wages would be paid in three installments. The first installment, one-third of the total, was to be paid on November 2, after which all workers would resume work. The second installment, one-third, was to be paid on November 4, and the third installment was to be paid on November 10. It was a prerequisite that wages would not be in arrears in the future. Other demands were to be resolved by the Party and government agencies within one week.

City News 198

Guan Sheng Yuan's Mobile Store

Mobile stores have been popular in Europe and America for a long time. Supplying what is available in one location to meet the needs of another is a good business practice. However, in our country, due to the road construction still being in its nascent stage, this type of mobile store has not yet appeared. The Guan Sheng Yuan Food Company in this city has always paid attention to the flow and display of goods. Recently, imitating the European and American mobile store model, they have ingeniously commissioned a store-style automobile from the United States. It has now been transported to Shanghai and assembled. The first trip was to Haining and Hangzhou for sales and exhibitions. During the National Day celebration at the city government, the vehicle was used to prepare and sell tea and snacks, which was very convenient and well-received by the viewers. According to the company's general manager, Mr. Chen, the vehicle will be used to provide tea and snacks for meetings held by various sectors at the company.

Luxurious fabrics such as wool crepe have traditionally been imported from overseas. The Pioneer of Domestic Buttons

Yu Jun Qiankang, who studied chemistry and industrial arts in Japan, has a deep understanding of various emerging industries. After returning to China, he held important positions in major factories. This summer, Mr. Yu deeply felt that the clothing of Chinese people is becoming increasingly Westernized, and most of the buttons are imported, resulting in significant annual leakage of funds. To remedy this situation, he raised funds to establish the Tiancheng Button Factory in Shanghai's East Gelan Road, Haizhou Road, Zhensheng Lane. The factory uses new machines to manufacture various types of buttons, and the goods have now begun to be shipped, marking the beginning of domestic buttons.

Art Exhibition 199

Art Exhibition of the Owner of Xiao Zhilian Studio

Mr. Shen Shiying, the owner of Xiao Zhilian Studio, is currently employed at the Qianyi Enterprise Bank in this city. The company was founded by prominent businessmen Wang Boyuan, Wang Zhongyun, Chen Xiaodie, He Gusheng, and Liang Chenlan. Recently, a technical cooperation association has been organized, and the management is thriving with many talented individuals. Mr. Shen has loved art since childhood and has a passion for epigraphy, calligraphy, and painting. He has collected many famous works. In the past, he studied watercolor and oil painting with the famous French painter Xu Beihong. He also felt ashamed that Chinese people did not appreciate Chinese painting, so he studied with famous Chinese painters Jiang Hanting and Zhao Shuru. He studied diligently and has become proficient. His horse paintings are particularly inspired by his teacher Zhao Shuru. Now, his works created during his spare time, such as imitations of Xinluo Shanren's screen albums, imitations of Nantian's flower paintings, and imitations of Song Dynasty horses, are exhibited at the Chinese Painting Association at the Chinese Art Exhibition. Mr. Shen is always busy with his work, and outsiders rarely see his masterpieces. Therefore, his limited works are even more precious.

Movies 200

"Dragon and Phoenix Dance" Returns

"Dragon and Phoenix Dance," the giant Ufa film that once caused a sensation in Shanghai last year, is scheduled to be re-released today (Wednesday) at the Carlton Cinema. The film is set against the backdrop of the most famous event in Western history, the Congress of Vienna, and depicts a romantic love story of Russian Emperor Alexander I. The leading actress, Lilian Harvey, became famous for this film, which attracted the attention of Hollywood producers, leading to her being signed by Fox Film Corporation for a large sum of money. The supporting actors, Henry Garat (now Jenny Gaynor's new screen lover), Erdan Gowa, and Conner Wade, are all top stars of the era. This film is nothing less than a foreign screen version of "Dragon and Phoenix Play," and the magnificent scenery is particularly innovative. Those who have not seen this film should not miss it.

Weather Report 203

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday was: Cloudy and rainy weather. Along the coast and in the north, the southerly or southwesterly winds will shift to westerly or northwesterly winds. There are strong northeasterly seasonal winds in the Taiwan Strait. The weather in the northern part of the China Sea is deteriorating due to a secondary low-pressure center moving westward northeast of the Macclesfield Islands towards the coast of Annam. The hurricane east of the Macclesfield Islands is moving northwest-westward. The center of the former was at 6 AM this morning at 13 degrees north latitude and 113 degrees east longitude, within 120 miles, and the center of the latter was at 2 PM this afternoon at 8 degrees north latitude and 137 degrees east longitude, within 120 miles. The wind force of both is unknown. Also, in the 24 hours before 3 PM yesterday, the temperature in this city was: highest 72.1, lowest 45.0. On the same day last year, the highest was 76.1, and the lowest was 51.1.

Provincial Girls' and Elementary School Boy Scouts Grand Camp and Review Closed Yesterday; Overall Scores: Girls' Middle School Group, 60th Regiment First Place (Provincial Yangzhong); Girls' Elementary School Group, 166th Regiment First Place (Zhenjiang Primary Schools); Elementary School Group, 356th Regiment First Place (Jiangyin Junyong) 209

The provincial girls' and elementary school Boy Scout grand review and camping event concluded yesterday. This morning, each troop dismantled their camps one after another. The campsite, which was previously crowded with tents, returned to its desolate appearance. The closing ceremony was held at the Provincial Party Headquarters at 4 p.m. Approximately hundreds of guests from all walks of life and Boy Scouts attended. After the ceremony, Zhou Shaozhen of the Provincial Party Committee,

The Chairman Reported, briefly stating: "This camping review has brought Boy Scouts from various regions together in one place. Everyone can learn from the strengths of others and discard their own weaknesses. Today, we are awarding prizes. I hope that those who receive prizes will not be arrogant, and those who do not receive prizes will not be discouraged. These prizes are all donated by various organizations and important figures. They have high expectations for all of you children. I hope you will all work harder upon returning." Following this, Chen Bangcai, the Secretary-General, reported on the scores of each group and the distribution of prizes.

Prizes Were Awarded, with Yangzhou and Zhenjiang winning the most awards. Cheers erupted, and the grand review and camping event, which had reached its peak, concluded with the sound of military music.

Local News

Chinese Painting Society and Xueyi Society to Host Chinese Art Exhibition Opening Tomorrow 224

The Chinese Art Exhibition, hosted by the Chinese Painting Society and the Chinese Xueyi Society, will be held from tomorrow (November 2nd) to the 12th at the Chinese Xueyi Society on Jin Shenfu Road and Aimeiyu Xian Road. The exhibition will include more than 500 pieces of fine art, including traditional Chinese paintings, calligraphy, sculpture, fine art photography, arts and crafts, architecture, oil paintings, and watercolors. Famous Shanghai painters have contributed to the exhibition, and artists from as far away as Fujian, Guangdong, and Wuhan have also participated. Tomorrow at 9 a.m., artists and members of the press will be invited to visit.

Municipal Education Bureau to Hold Civic Lecture Tomorrow; Teachers and Staff of Primary and Secondary Schools Should Attend 225

According to Article 10 of the Municipal Education Bureau's Civic Training Center Planning Scheme for Primary and Secondary Schools, experts will be hired to give various civic training lectures. The first lecture will be on "Civic Hygiene," and Dr. Li Tingan, Director of the Bureau of Health, has been invited to speak. The lecture is scheduled for 3:30 p.m. tomorrow (Thursday) in the auditorium of Wuben Girls' Middle School on Huangjia Que Road in Ximen. All civic training teachers and staff from municipal and private primary and secondary schools in the city must attend and sign in. The Bureau previously issued a notice to be posted on bulletin boards and in the Educational Weekly.

Educators from Shangqiu Come to Shanghai for Observation 226

Shangqiu is an important hub in eastern Henan and was formerly the seat of the prefecture government. Its educational undertakings should be the best in the county. However, in recent years, it has suffered many disasters, so the education in the county has been severely damaged. Mr. Chen Yansheng, a young man in the county who is enthusiastic about running education, donated 2,000 yuan after the major disaster last year to build a large bridge. Therefore, the Construction Department of Henan Province had a plaque with the words "Enthusiastic about Public Welfare." In the autumn of the Republic of China's 21st year (1932), he donated 2,000 yuan to found a complete primary school, named "Yansheng Primary School." Since its opening, the results have been outstanding. Recently, in order to seek improvement, Mr. Chen has specially accompanied Ms. Shang Kunhua, a member of the school board, and Mr. Sun Juting, the principal, to Beijing and Shanghai to visit various schools for inspiration. It is said that Mr. Chen and others have completed their visits in Beijing and arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday. They will visit various schools.

Sports

Physical Education Specialized School in Preparation by Ministry of Education—Central Stadium as Site—However, National Military Physical Education School Also Plans to Use Central Stadium 227

(Nanjing, 31st Telegram) The Ministry of Education's Sports Committee is planning to establish a specialized physical education school and use the Central Stadium as its site. At the same time, Commission Chairman Jiang of the Military Commission is paying attention to military education and also intends to borrow the field to establish a National Military Physical Education Specialized School. He has also sent a letter to the Ministry of Education to negotiate the loan. The Ministry of Education is concerned that the specialized physical education school has financial difficulties and cannot afford to build another site. It has sent a letter to the Military Commission to inquire about the plans of the Military Physical Education School. If the content is similar to that of the specialized physical education school, it would be better to merge it with the Military Commission for joint management.

Two Basketball Games Tonight: Philippine Overseas Chinese vs. Jinan; 7 p.m. at the Chinese Basketball Hall; Also, St. John's vs. McLeans at St. John's; Tomorrow Night: Philippine Overseas Chinese vs. Qianghua Team 228

Philippine Overseas Chinese vs. Jinan The Philippine Overseas Chinese basketball team made its debut the night before last and defeated Datong, the champion of the Jiangda League. Tonight at 7 p.m., they will play against Jinan University for the second time. The location is still the Chinese Basketball Hall. The Philippines is known for its swiftness and skill in combat. Jinan is known for its fierceness and bravery. This meeting will be a thrilling battle. The referee will be Mr. Wu Zhitang. Also, tomorrow night, the Philippine team will play against the Qianghua team, which is composed of students and alumni of St. John's University.

St. John's vs. McLeans The West Youth Basketball League is about to begin. In order to prepare for winning the championship, each basketball team is sharpening its swords and actively preparing for battle. The Vatican King St. John's University team is scheduled to play a friendly match with McLeans tonight. The location is in Vatican King Ferry. Both teams are strong and promising.

Fifth Municipal Elementary School Games Scheduled to Be Held; To Be Held for Three Days Starting November 9th; Location: Municipal First Public Stadium 229

The Fifth Shanghai Municipal Joint Elementary School Games, sponsored by the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education, will be held for three days starting November 9th at the Municipal First Public Stadium on Dalin Road in Ximen. All municipal elementary schools and registered elementary schools must participate. The sports program includes track and field events and group exercises. Each school must submit its participating program to the Municipal Bureau of Education before 5 p.m. this Saturday (4th) for allocation. The combined exercise teaching materials and the Sports Games song, the athlete registration form, etc., will all be published in the newspaper tomorrow. The notice to each school is recorded below:

(1) The Sports Games song and combined exercise teaching materials will be distributed to each school by the conference. They must practice them thoroughly. (2) The number of athletes in each school's track and field competition is limited to four per group per event. Each athlete may participate in three sports. (3) Track and field athletes are divided into three groups, A, B, and C. Those weighing 90 pounds or more are in Group A, those weighing 80 pounds or more but less than 90 pounds are in Group B, and those weighing less than 80 pounds are in Group C. (4) Track and field events: Boys' Group (Group A): 100 meters, 200 meters, 400 meters, 800 meters, 110-meter low hurdles, high jump, long jump, 6-pound shot put, pole vault; (Group B): 100 meters, 200 meters, 400 meters, high jump, long jump, 4-pound shot put; (Group C): 100 meters, 200 meters, high jump, long jump, 3-pound shot put. Girls' Group (all girls' groups): 50 meters, standing long jump, softball throw. (5) After an athlete competes in a certain group in the previous event, they may not move up or down any group for the next event. If discovered, the points earned by the athlete will be cancelled. (6) During track and field competitions, Group A athletes may wear spiked running shoes and running shoes. Other groups are not allowed to wear them. (7) Group exercises should show all the usual teaching materials, and the time for each session should not exceed 20 minutes. (8) Each school with 12 or more grades should perform at least two sessions of group exercises, and those with less than 12 grades should perform at least one session. (9) At least six-tenths of the students in each school should perform the group exercises. (10) The equipment used in the group exercises should be prepared by each school. (11) The group exercises in each school should be in short uniforms. (12) The list of athletes for group exercises and track and field events in each school and the registration form for track and field events must be filled out and submitted to the Preparatory Office before 5 p.m. on November 4th. Late submissions will not be accepted. (13) Athletes should arrive at the meeting before 8 a.m. in the morning and before 1 p.m. in the afternoon every day. (14) If any school has any application matters regarding the competition, they should contact the Director of the Meeting Affairs and should not protest to the referees. (15) The track and field sports rules shall be implemented with reference to the rules recently approved by the Chinese National Sports Association.

Youth Handball Ranking Tournament: Sun Daosheng Retreats to Third Place 232

Last night at the Youth Handball Court, the audience was packed. Word had spread that Sun and Hong, two famous players, were coming to watch. At 5:30 PM, Hong Yukui and Sun Daosheng arrived at the court one after the other. After a brief warm-up, the match began. In the first game, Hong took the initiative and won several points in a row. Sun followed closely, smashing the ball back and forth, showcasing his skills. However, Hong was physically strong and played more and more aggressively, ultimately winning the first game with a score of 21 to 10. In the second game, Sun improved slightly, and the score was very close. However, Hong changed his strategy and gained many points in a row, leaving Sun powerless to retaliate, and Hong won the second game 21 to 12, rising to second place.

Today's schedule at 5:30 PM: (1) Hua Fenggang vs. Cai Tongshou at Court A; (2) Yu Guanghan vs. Yan Peida at Court B.

YMCA Indoor Swimming Pool Open 233

The Shanghai YMCA, recognizing the backward state of swimming in our country and the urgent need for improvement, has spared no expense in installing hot water pipes in the YMCA swimming pool, in addition to vigorously promoting the sport in the fall. This allows members of the public to practice swimming in all seasons. The installation is now complete, and the water and room temperatures are comfortable. Experiments have proven it to be satisfactory. It is scheduled to officially open at 5:00 PM this afternoon. Non-members are also welcome. For the sake of popularization, there are no restrictions on gender, but the times for women will be announced separately.

Qingzhong Alumni Basketball Team Defeats the Eagle Team 234

The renowned Eagle Team, by invitation from the Youth Association Middle School Alumni Team, played a friendly match yesterday in the YMCA gymnasium on Sichuan Road. Their excellent ball skills and agile coordination made them formidable opponents for the Qingzhong Alumni Team, but their guards were slightly lacking. As a result, they lost to the Qingzhong Alumni Team with a score of 48 to 41.

World's Top Ten Tennis Players: Opinions of British Expert Meyer; Japan's Sato Ranks Third 235

(London Correspondence) The 1933 tennis season showed some recurring and confusing facts. The dominance of the United States and France in the world for thirteen years has been interrupted. In the women's world, Mrs. Moody has encountered her first failure after a long period of dominance. According to observations by British tennis expert Meyer, the top ten male and female tennis players in the world this year should be listed as follows:

▲Men

(1) Crawford (Australia) (2) Perry (England)

(3) Sato (Japan) (4) Austin (England)

(5) Vines (USA) (6) Cochet (France)

(7) Shields (USA) (8) Wood (USA)

(5) Cramm (Germany) (10) Stoefen (USA)

▲Women

(1) Mrs. Moody (USA) (2) Miss Jacobs (USA)

(3) Miss Round (England) (4) Mrs. Krawinkel (Germany)

(5) Miss Scriven (England) (6) Mrs. Mathieu (France)

(7) Miss Pfeiffer (USA) (8) Miss Nuthall (England)

(9) Mrs. Bayer (Switzerland) (10) Miss Marble (USA)

The biggest difference in the men's ranking is the rise of Japan's Sato to third place, probably due to his Wimbledon performance and his victory over Vines and Perry. Sato and Buichi won the finals in doubles at Wimbledon. Austin's fourth place is entirely due to his Davis Cup performance, but Vines did win the finals at Wimbledon.

World Olympic Branch: All-European Games to be Held in Italy Next Year, Every Four Years 236

(London Correspondence) The World Olympic Games are held every four years. Now, in addition to that, another international sports event is added, as a branch of the World Olympic Games. According to the resolution of the International Amateur Athletic Federation, the first European Games will be held in Italy next year, 1934.

Every Four Years 237

This type of sports event will also be held every four years. The competition will be divided into three days. In each event, only two athletes from each country can participate, for a total of six places. Points are calculated as 6, 5, 4, 3, 2, 1, with the first place getting six points. The country hosting the games will be responsible for providing food and lodging for the participating athletes. Four percent of the games' income will go to the International Amateur Athletic Federation.

Britain Feels Most Inconvenienced 238

It is not certain whether this resolution and method will be welcomed by the world. Britain feels most inconvenienced because it coincides with the All-British Empire Games every four years, which will inevitably be even busier. But in any case, the Empire Games will definitely be held at White City in London next year.

Free Talk

The Entertainment of Farmers 240

— Tang Tao

A fellow villager came, and when talking about the recent situation in the countryside, he first let out a long sigh, followed by a mouthful of complaints. He said that even things that could bring some joy were gone.

A few years ago, when there was a relatively good harvest, it was common to put on a few plays or hold a temple fair to relax the spirit. And each time, there would be crowds of people eager to watch the fun; it seemed that using one's own sweat to please one's own eyes and ears was more enjoyable.

However, the sweat and blood of the farmers should not be spent on themselves after all.

Temple fairs and plays were eventually interfered with. The reason for the interference, I heard at first, was to eliminate superstition. But at each temple fair or theater, there were more people than gods, and people who understood happiness better than the Buddhas. Probably in the eyes of the interferers, these people had all turned into Buddhas, so watching plays and temple fairs was close to superstition and had to be stopped!

Recently, a national crisis came out of nowhere, and the reason changed accordingly. Except for dances that could save the country, any kind of entertainment should be abolished. However, this "should" has now proven to apply only to remote rural areas.

In my hometown, there used to be dragon lantern festivals, partly to embellish the prosperous times and partly to show "sharing happiness with the people." Now, because the national crisis is in full swing, the adults and gentlemen are worried, and even the rural farmers have to wear mourning faces.

But not long ago, I heard that it could be relaxed again, probably if it was organized by the government or merchants. The purpose was to promote national salvation, and the tickets cost two dimes, but the plays performed were mostly stories like "Diao Liu's Killing Her Son to Avenge."

But business was not very prosperous.

After being interfered with, and then having to pay two dimes for a ticket, the farmers' lonely hearts no longer thought of entertainment.

Li Zhuowu, the Novel Critic 241

— Yu Shixia

Ancient vernacular novels, from the Tang and Five Dynasties Bianwen, to the Song and Yuan Pinghua, mostly came from the hands of storytellers in the city streets, and it seems that those self-proclaimed erudite literati at that time never paid attention to them. It was not until the Ming Dynasty that many famous literati began to pay attention to novels, either creating, editing, or commenting on them. For example, the short stories "Three Words" and "Two Slaps" were edited by Feng Menglong and Ling Mengchu, and perhaps they also contained their own creations. The chapter novels "Water Margin" and "Romance of the Three Kingdoms" are said to have been written by Shi Nai'an and Luo Guanzhong, who were all from the late Yuan Dynasty. "Journey to the West" was written by Wu Cheng'en, and "Jin Ping Mei" is suspected to be the work of Wang Shizhen. As for novel critics, the most famous were Li Zhuowu and Zhong Bojing in the early period, and Jin Shengtan in the later period. Mr. Zhou Zuoren, in his lecture on "The Origins of New Literature," has a very clear and concise introduction to Zhong Bojing. Jin Shengtan is known to almost every household because of his commentary on "Romance of the Three Kingdoms," which is extremely popular. Now I want to talk about Li Zhuowu.

The most novels attributed to Li Zhuowu's commentary are "Water Margin," "Romance of the Three Kingdoms," "Journey to the West," as well as "Kongkong Huan," "Longtu Gong'an," and "Embroidered Couch Wild History." There is also "The Romance of Seventy-Two Dynasties and Four Books Figures," also titled "Mr. Li Zhuowu's Secret Book." Why was he so fond of novels? Speaking of him, he was truly a strange person. He passed the imperial examination and served as a proofreader and prefect. He was originally from Jinjiang, Quanzhou, and because he was friendly with Geng Ziyong of Huang'an, he resided in Huang'an after resigning from office. Later, he moved to Longtan Lake in Macheng, where he studied and lectured. One day, his head itched, so he shaved his head and became a monk. He preached tirelessly, and women also came to listen. Some said, "Women have short vision, not short learning." He said, "It is acceptable to say that people have genders, but how can it be said that vision has genders? It is acceptable to say that vision has lengths, but how can it be said that men's vision is always long and women's vision is always short? Moreover, those who come for the Dharma are not as good as men." Originally, Zhuowu was upright and solitary, intelligent and outstanding, quick-witted and eloquent, and shocked people with his unconventional ideas. His academic tenets were between Confucianism and Buddhism. He hated corrupt scholars as gentlemen and often criticized Confucius. He said: "Heaven gives birth to one person, and each person has their own use, not needing to take from Confucius to be sufficient. If one must take from Confucius, then before the millennia before Confucius, could one not be a person?" He believed that for thousands of years in the Han, Tang, and Song dynasties, there was no right or wrong, "because everyone took Confucius's right and wrong as their own, so there was never right or wrong." Since he refused to learn from Confucius and instead took Confucius's right and wrong as his own, he was naturally hated by those eight-legged essayists and corrupt scholars of the time. He was a comet with boundless brilliance in the thinking world of the time, and only one person like Wang Chong. Jiao Hong and Zhuowu were contemporaries, and he was a scholar with extensive reading who looked down on people, but he alone admired Zhuowu. He said:

Zhuowu is noble and pure, like Mount Tai, solemn and inviolable. Listening to his words, one feels cold and all the dust is gone. The doubts of the masses cannot overcome the belief of the wise and heroic; the uncertainty of the doubters cannot overcome the determination of the believers. Although he may not be a saint, he can bear the word "mad" and sit in the second seat of a saint.

Zhuowu's books were first burned in the 30th year of Wanli, at the request of Zhang Wenda. They were burned again in the fifth year of Tianqi, at the request of censor Wang Yaliang. Only the many novels attributed to his commentary escaped this violence. He was impeached and imprisoned by Zhang Wenda for being an "evil person" and died by cutting his throat. We must not forget that he was an eccentric who opposed Confucius and traditional thought, and he was not bound by traditional literature, so he was willing to put his mind to commenting on novels. However, the fact that people wanted to attribute their commentary on novels to him was not without reason. Zhou Liangong, in his "Book Shadows from the Tree House," said that there was "Ye Wentong, a famous painter from Wuxi. He read a lot, had talent and feelings, and paid attention to the learning of the two clans [Confucianism and Buddhism], so he had strange behavior... When the burning of books was prevalent in Wenling [Zhuowu], various people in the workshops borrowed the name of Wenling to sell their works, such as the First and Second Commentaries on the Four Books, Water Margin, Pipa, Baiyue, etc., all came from Wentong's hands." Perhaps the novels attributed to Li Zhuowu's commentary include those by Zhuowu himself and those falsely attributed by Ye Wentong.

Two Korean Children's Songs 242

— Translated by Mu Mutian

(1) Crow (Kim Yong-jak)

Every day when I come back from the factory,

On the hill by the seaside at dusk,

Wearing black clothes

A flock of many crows

Cries "Caw!" "Caw!"

Other birds

Have returned to their nests,

Only the crows gather at sunset.

Do they have night school?

Or are they holding a meeting there because of some injustice and dissatisfaction?

Their gathering at dusk

Is truly like our night school.

(2) The Pastor and the Swallows (Park Aji)

The bearded pastor in our village,

When children bullied the swallows,

Rebuked them, saying

"It is not allowed to bully the cute swallows."

Now that bearded bastard

No longer a pastor, is raising bees.

As a result, he cruelly used a pole

To kill the swallow that took away the bees.

"Why kill the cute swallows?"

We asked the bearded man.

The bearded man blushed and said nothing.

Strange, strange, truly strange.

Breakout (Continued) 243

— Shi Zhecun

I clearly remember that there is indeed a story in the "Yan Family Instructions" about someone teaching their children to learn the Xianbei language and play the Pipa, but I also remember that there is a sentence underneath: "I also do not want you all to do this." It can be seen that Yan Zhitui did not encourage his children to read foreign books. Today, Mr. Feng has made a correction, and after correcting this story, he said: "Mr. Shi Zhecun is indeed combining the two typical examples of ten and Yan's family." This, I don't understand. Did I also introduce another work that should be to young people? If Mr. Feng's is based on "reading foreign books yourself is helping others learn the Xianbei language," then I have nothing to say.

Mr. seems to be a character who wants to defend the orthodoxy of Confucianism, otherwise why would he be so critical of Yan Zhitui's influence from Buddhism! Why would he be so dissatisfied with me reading a biography of Sakyamuni! There are two points that can be raised here: (1) Can the value of the book "Yan Family Instructions" be completely erased because of "returning to the heart"? Moreover, although Yan is advocating for Buddhism, he does not encourage leaving the world and escaping from reality. He is simply listing the points where Buddhism and can coexist without conflict, and adopting the Buddhist theory of retribution to supplement the inadequacy of Confucian moral teachings. This can also be said to be equivalent to people today quoting words from the "Bible" or "Koran." (2) My reading of a Buddhist biography is equivalent to reading a "Biography of Muhammad" or a "Biography of Christ." I have no intention of converting to Buddhism, nor do I have the intention of persuading others to study Buddhism. However, Mr. Feng's article says that it is my "way of life." How wonderful! I cannot help but take a copy of "Hundred Sutras" published by a certain Mr. Shejin on my desk and use it as a fellow believer.

In the past, although I had a slightly idealistic tone in my writing with Mr. Feng, I did indeed express respect. However, after seeing the article "Missing the Mark," he actually cursed me as a "gangster on the foreign field." The sound of gnashing teeth is almost audible. Although I am "evil," I dare not be so evil as to repay him with a comparable curse. I will just use a ready-made sentence: "Ten years of writing in the literary world, winning the name of gangster on the foreign field" is not worth mentioning, but I think Mr. Feng will regret it. Today, after reading "Correction of Missing the Mark," I feel that Mr. Feng's so-called "unprovoked scriptures, self-speculation, withdrawal, should, is just right for me to."

(Note) The two headlines on the "Great Evening News" were not added by me. I have no "position" and do not want to cause "Zhuangzi" and "Wen Xuan" to argue with each other because of me.

The above is a reply to Mr. Feng Zhiyu □ Complete (27th)

My Protest 244

— Gao Ming

In the article signed "Jusheng" published in "Free Talk" on the 27th, it is said that "Opium War" was written by Tomoyoshi Murayama, not by Kan Eguchi, so I (Gao Ming) made a mistake, etc. This really confuses me. As far as I know, "Opium War" was indeed originally written by Kan Eguchi, and Tomoyoshi Murayama was at most just a reviser. I have not "consulted" the Chinese translation of "The First Flag of Europe." If the translator did not state on it that this thing was originally written by Kan Eguchi, then it only shows the translator's ignorance.

The Two Brothers (15) 245

— Guy de Maupassant, translated by Li Weike

Pierre asked:

"So you were very familiar with him before, with this Malaisha?"

The father replied:

"Of course, he came to our house every night to play; but you must remember that on holidays, he came to school to pick you up, and after dinner he often took you back to school. Ah, that's right, he was the one who went to find the doctor the morning Jean was born! When your mother felt the pain, he happened to be eating at our house. We immediately knew that your mother was about to give birth, and he rushed to find the doctor. In his haste, he even wore my hat instead of his own. Because we often laughed about this afterwards, I still remember it. Perhaps he remembered these trivial things when he was dying: Since he had no heirs, he thought, 'Ah, I contributed greatly to the birth of this little one, I will leave my property to him.'"

Madam Roland sat in a reclining chair, as if immersed in memories of the past. She murmured, as if confessing her heart:

"Ah! He was an upright friend, a very familiar, very loyal friend, a person hard to find in this day and age."

Jean stood up and said:

"I'm going out for a walk."

His father was surprised and wanted to stop him, because they had something to talk about, they had to plan some things, decide some things. But they still had plenty of time to discuss things before they took possession of the inheritance.

So he went out, because he wanted to leave everyone and think alone. Then Pierre also said he was going out, and a few minutes later, followed his brother.

When only Father Roland and his woman were left together, he hugged her in his arms, kissed her ten times on each cheek, and to repay her for the criticism she often gave him, he said to her:

"Look, dear, it was not a loss for us to move here, recover my health, and stop staying in Paris to be beasts of burden for the children, because wealth really fell from the sky to us."

She looked very serious and said:

"This wealth really fell from the sky to Jean, but what about Pierre?"

"Pierre! But he is a doctor, he can earn it himself... earn some money, and his brother will definitely help him a little."

"No, he won't accept it. And this inheritance is for Jean, only for Jean alone. In this way, Pierre will be far less wealthy than his brother."

The honest man seemed to feel difficulty:

"Then we will leave him a little more in the will in the future."

"No. That's not a very fair way either."

He exclaimed:

"Ah! Then what should we do, ha! What can I do about this? You are always looking for all kinds of unpleasant thoughts. You want to spoil everything for me. Ah, I'm going to sleep. Good night. In any case, this is always a good fortune, a very good fortune!"

So he ran off to sleep happily, without caring about anything, without a word of regret for the friend who had died so generously.

Madam Roland began to meditate again in front of the burnt-out oil lamp.

A Glimpse of the Completion of Long-Term Contracts 251

Yesterday was the final settlement period for this term's long-term contracts. All procedures for entry, exit, deposit, and arrears were completed. According to reports from industry insiders, the estimated amount of transfers for this term was more than 31 million. New transactions were 7 to 8 million, and recoveries were 5 to 6 million. Deposit transfers amounted to more than 10 million. The amount that should be recovered but could not be repaid, and seemed to have become bad debts, totaled more than 3 million.
