Shanghai Chinese Yarn and Cloth Exchange Cotton Delivery Inspection Rules 261

The Shanghai Chinese Yarn and Cloth Exchange has revised the cotton delivery inspection rules, totaling 23 articles, which will be implemented from November. Excerpts of the main points are recorded below, but the full text published by the exchange shall prevail.

(Article 1) Cotton delivery shall be requested for inspection by the delivering broker at any time after the 10th of each month (weighing must be carried out after the 20th) and no later than two days before the monthly delivery. (Article 2) The order of inspection shall be carried out according to the order of request. (Article 3) When the cotton is inspected, if the pattern matches the standard, each 100 dan, such as Renji cloth bags, is about 85 bags per lot. Hanyang cotton has 4 tubes, each tube weighing about 1 pound (and so on). If it is a machine-baled large package of about 4 dan, there are about 25 to 27 bags per lot, totaling 100 dan. Two bags must be opened for sampling, and two tubes of cotton samples weighing about 2 pounds must be taken. If a lot has two brands, open two more bags and take two more tubes to separately inspect the amount of moisture. (Article 5) The moisture content of cotton shall be 12% as the standard. If it is 13%, the price must be reduced by 1%. If it exceeds 13%, it is unqualified. (Article 6) Cotton delivered, regardless of the type of packaging, can be delivered. (Article 8) Cotton that fails the inspection shall be replaced by the deliverer as soon as possible, and the replaced goods shall be delivered no later than one day before delivery. If the inspection still fails, and delivery cannot be made the next day, it shall be deemed a breach of contract. (Article 10) The validity period of the cotton inspection certificate is limited to 7 days after the monthly delivery is completed. (Article 12) If the delivering broker considers the cotton to be unsuitable after inspection, he may submit reasons to request re-inspection. The re-inspection fee is 70 yuan per 100 dan, 105 yuan within 5 times, and 140 yuan within 10 times, which shall be paid in advance by the requester. If the judgment result confirms that the inspection was inappropriate, it shall be refunded by the exchange. (Article 16) If the cotton passes the inspection but is not delivered, a water inspection fee of 0.03 silver yuan per dan shall be charged, and a weighing fee of 0.03 silver yuan shall be paid (weighing labor is calculated separately). (Article 17) Cotton delivery shall be in units of 100 dan, and the remainder shall be omitted.

Spring and Autumn

Half a Buddhist Scripture Pacifies the World 270

— Yongzi

Buddhism prohibits killing, supposedly out of a reluctance to sacrifice the lives of livestock to satisfy one's gluttony. Extending this compassion to livestock, although showing no pity for plants, which also possess "life," and unhesitatingly cooking and consuming them, the difference between fifty steps and a hundred steps means we cannot worship the greatness of those who only escaped fifty steps. Therefore, although Buddhism's prohibition of killing does not extend to plants, which also have life, we must admire the spirit of Buddhists who do not eat animal meat, which is ultimately superior to those who cannot even do this and adhere to the "survival of the fittest" theory.

The core of Chinese culture lies in "compassion." Although Confucianism, Buddhism, and Taoism stand as a tripod, they all retain "the heart of compassion." To quote a phrase, it could be said to be "the way of benevolent governance." This is naturally the "magnanimity of a great nation" that a "land of propriety and deference" should possess, and it is also a powerful underlying factor preventing the Chinese nation from being eliminated by foreign races. During the Five Barbarians Rebellion, the Huns and Tatars who ruled over China ultimately had to return power to the descendants of the Yellow Emperor, which is a good example. Moreover, all those who ruled over China and enslaved the descendants of the Yellow Emperor eventually could not escape being assimilated by the Chinese nation, fulfilling the Buddhist "law of karma," because intending to enslave and destroy another nation is acting against the way of heaven, planting a "bad cause," which leads to the "bad effect" of being assimilated. Therefore, although India and Korea have been conquered, if the end of the world does not come, there will surely be a day when they will restore their lands.

Entrusting all great matters to Heaven" is not only the most important page of life philosophy, but also the essence of political philosophy. Napoleon, Louis XIII, and Wilhelm II, shouting and scolding, clearly never studied the great principles of "non-birth and non-death" and "non-contention with the world." In modern times, figures like Mussolini, Hitler, Stalin, and Araki, how could any of them understand "the cycle of retribution" and "the manifestation of heavenly principles"? Only those who have no "ambition to expand territory" and "are indifferent to gains and losses" can endure some "immediate losses" without fear and sit back to collect "debts in the next life."

Half of the Analects can govern the world, but this "world" only refers to the "world" within the four seas. Only half of a Buddhist scripture can pacify the "world" beyond the four seas and turn weapons into silk. Therefore, not only did Commander Wu Yu and Commander Sun put down their butcher knives, read scriptures, and convert to Buddhism, but famous figures in Europe and America also crossed the ocean to China to take vows at Mount Baohua and become Buddhist disciples. It seems that those who will pacify the world in the future will not be anything other than half a Buddhist scripture.

The Groans of Peasants in Bandit Areas 271

— Yun Si

Shanghai is promoting the use of domestic goods by the public, designating this year as "National Products Year." Meanwhile, in XX Province, the unexterminated bandits and communists are harming the local people. The military and civilians of that province are united in heart and mind, designating this year as "Bandit Extermination Year," to show their determination not to coexist with the bandits! However, the bandit forces are still rampant, and the people are still suffering. Yesterday, I met a friend from XX Province who brought me a lot of news about XX Province. I am now recording the essentials of what he told me to represent the groans of the peasants in the bandit areas.

Fields with no hope of autumn harvest always present a bleak, withered, and yellow face. The villagers are not as busy as in previous autumns, only wandering around, looking here and there, or returning to what they call "houses," which are bare and empty. The children, with gaunt faces, say to their fathers, "I'm hungry!" and to their mothers, "I'm cold!" But their parents, besides sighs, no longer say excitedly as before, "The gold in the fields is our clothing! It's our white rice!" With no harvest in the fields, what about the "National Salvation Donation" and the "Bandit Extermination Military Donation"? These good-sounding names are still the obligations of the farmers.

The law-abiding farmers, besides closing their eyes and starving to death alive in their "houses," have no other evil thoughts. Sometimes, one also sees members of the relief committee sticking their heads out of car windows to look outside. They have even used the mouths that have eaten shark fin soup at fifty yuan a meal and the lips that have smoked cigars at one yuan each to say, "Relief! Relief!" But when the green smoke of the cigars drifts out in wisps, the echoes of "Relief! Relief!" also come to an end. The stubborn farmers, deluded by the noble name of "not willing to starve to death," then take the risk of joining the bandits' ranks. Although they know this thing is unwanted, for the sake of living, they can't worry about so much.

The peasants in the bandit areas have all abandoned their homes, which are devoid of possessions, to live a life of fleeing with wives and scattering children. The wife experiences cold wind and dew, and a dismal moon hangs high. The deserted village, besides the barking of the few chickens and dogs left behind by the owners, has no other sound. The withered crops in the fields appear exceptionally desolate under the moonlight. The autumn insects chirping are no longer appreciated by anyone, and no one will compose a second "Autumn Sounds Rhapsody."

Bending and Stretching 272

— Hu Liwen

Being able to bend and stretch is the way to not be a complete man, as the ancients all say. A person must listen in all directions and see in all places. Even if someone bullies you, you must first see what kind of person the other party is. If it is someone as skinny as dry noodles, then you can be honest and rude, using your old fist to vent your anger. If you unfortunately encounter a shrewd ghost, then you must act according to the situation, because if you are reckless, you are bound to suffer.

Only bending and not stretching, that kind of person has no prospects. Only stretching and not bending, that kind of person is also an impetuous brave man. Having no prospects, then there is only the qualification to be a slave. The bravery of an impetuous man does not have a good result. However, retreating step by step, leading to the disaster of losing one's life, that is not as good as only stretching and not bending! What is sad is that the people of the country do not see this and still resolutely consider themselves able to act according to the situation. What more can be said! What more can be said!

Autumn in the Countryside 273

— Jin Lou

In the countryside, as I tread the fine, even, and soft soil of the village, serenity and warmth are the hallmarks here. Under the boundless and crystalline sky, the clouds drift so leisurely, skimming over the eyebrow-like distant mountains, skimming over the red forests, skimming over the masts of the fishing boats flying small white flags...

Yellow wild chrysanthemums dot the quiet tombs along the road. Silver-colored lambs scatter about in the vast, desolate gardens, all looking so leisurely. Old yellow oxen lie in the haystacks, their mouths constantly grinding. Occasionally, a long moo from these clumsy creatures startles the small sparrows foraging for rice grains in the fields, causing them to fly together into the treetops...

Innocent and charming village children stand in twos and threes by the fences, singing their practiced local tunes, which are so moving! City people always cast curious glances whenever they pass by... "Look! Another person in a long gown is here!" they shout!

The golden haystacks in the fields are already piled high. Honest and simple old farmers puff diligently on their dry tobacco pipes as they work hard. Dry laughter sometimes emanates from them. Exchanging labor for harvest is their only source of joy...

Low thatched huts are embedded where the sky and earth meet, and wisps of smoke are faintly visible, seemingly upside down on the rooftops, lingering for a long time... Small white flags flutter from the treetops, the signs of village inns and teahouses... The scenery is so elegant and pleasant, with a beauty of serenity, an oriental charm, like a painting in Wang Wei's poems...

Many village women with blue cloth headscarves come and go in the fields, all deeply silent, bathed in the sea of autumn light. On each healthy-colored face, the joy of harvest is expressed! The women of the city are daughters of materialism, but they are daughters of nature.

By the small stream, village girls are pounding clothes on blue stones again. Vines clinging to the bridge railings flutter in their beautiful hair. The rushing stream crashes on the blue stones, producing the autumn melody of a zither. A small fish jumps out of the water with a "dong!" sound. Fine and lustrous silver scales reflect the autumn sunlight, flashing quickly before their eyes, making them think of the fishing nets they have woven themselves at home, which is so satisfying!

In the countryside, as I tread the fine, even, and soft soil of the village, serenity and warmth are the characteristics here!

Short Message 274

Society member Jiang Junyinqiu recently collaborated with three Wu-style calligraphers from Wu Xia, Wu Qingwang, Yu Jue, and Wu Jinxian, on a four-panel screen painting. Wu Qingwang's Zhen script is full, mellow, rounded, and pleasing. Yu Jue's cursive script demonstrates unrestrained brushwork, already renowned in the art world. Jinxian, although a rising star, excels in all four styles, with a particular focus on Han-style clerical script, striving to emulate Yuan Shou's style. Yinqiu, a writer from Zengsheng Society, specializes in seal script, with silver hooks and iron strokes, and a transcendent ancient flavor. Now, these four gentlemen have the elegant inclination to collaborate, and the affordable commission is offered to the public. Screen paintings measuring three to four feet per panel are priced at only five or six yuan, and five to six feet at only seven or eight yuan. This is a literary game, using it to form a connection through calligraphy. — Jian

Northeast Fourth Company Commander 275

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 18: Sending Tea with Pulsing Armpits Comforts the Husband; Hastily Leaving the Border, Forcing a Smile to Bid Farewell to Family

Some say that patriotism is a kind of superstition. As long as this idea of patriotism is instilled into the minds of the people, that person can completely sacrifice their life and property for the sake of patriotism. If people in the world had no such patriotic ideas, there would be no military wars or economic wars, and people would be much happier. In fact, this kind of patriotic superstition is not easily transmitted. Like Zhao Weng, he usually promotes patriotic ideas very much. But when his son is about to lead troops to the front line to fight for the country, he will feel twenty-four minutes of unease in his heart, feeling that the artillery fire is a merciless thing. His son is serving as a company commander, which is like the brothers going to the front line together, and there is no safe zone where they can dig to protect themselves. Therefore, although he feels uncomfortable in his heart, he still encourages his son in his mouth to contribute to the country. When he heard clearly that his son was going to Xifengkou to block the pass, which was far away from the Japanese army, his spirit suddenly perked up, and he kept shouting for Old Lady Yang in the outer courtyard. Jiang suddenly heard Zhao Weng shouting like this, and she was a little confused in her heart, so she immediately answered and walked to the backyard. Zhao Weng waited for her to enter the door, clapped his hands and said, "Now I understand, we don't have to worry so much. Ziqiang is not going out of Shanhaiguan, just to Xifengkou. This place is far away from the fighting place. To be honest, being stationed there is almost the same as being in the Xiyuan camp, it doesn't matter at all." (228)

Miscellaneous Complaints

Climate Change 276

— Xingbi

In our impression, above everything, a fiery, red-hot umbrella completely unfolds, roasting all living and non-living things alike, making them feel the same feverish heat!

Non-living things indeed have no way to resist; they can only endure this brutal threat, hardly daring to move at all.

Living birds and beasts, embracing a policy of non-resistance, can only shout and scream wildly, flying and running around, busy without end, each searching for shady places.

Humans are the spirits of all things. For the sake of livelihood, how can they shrink back and not strive and struggle?

In an instant, the future scene will make our eyes and bodies feel something absolutely opposite to the past. In this bleak scene, we can hear sounds like dragons roaring and tigers howling, and we suddenly feel that the clothes on our bodies are exceptionally thin. Sometimes, we even need to use the heat of fire to help us resist the invading cold!

Everything outside—flying—walking—is not easily encountered casually.

What lies before us—green—green—lofty—lush—covering a portion of the earth, we are afraid that we can only see a few dry, bald tree trunks. But on those branches, perhaps we can find a few yellow leaves that are about to fall but haven't yet!

Pine, bamboo, and plum are not afraid of the ravages of frost and snow, but instead show off their outstanding appearance triumphantly, surviving!

Silver snowflakes pile up on everything, reflecting a pure and bright world.

Small rivers and shallow ponds have actually turned from liquid to that glassy solid. Then, on the eaves, many transparent crystals are found, hanging there long and short!

In the middle of the past and the future is the present. This present, we must know, what kind of climate, what kind of situation is it?

The food in the bowls and cups has a smoke-like quality, rising up and lingering in the air. The clothes on our bodies are darker in color and thicker in texture!

A red—round—radiant sun gradually emerges from the fish-belly-colored morning light. Grasslands like green felt and leaves like green velvet have long been moistened by the clean, nourishing dew.

Farmers, barefoot and bent over, work in the green fields. There are also fishermen wearing mist and carrying bamboo hats, casting their fishing rods and nets on the autumn waters of the stream, watching intently—waiting—hoping—for the float to sink and the net to be submerged, not caring that the mist and bamboo hats on their bodies are as if they have gone through a fine rain!

The singing birds in the forest, the chirping cicadas among the trees, and the crickets chirping in the four walls, all, one after another, sing triumphant songs at this time, chanting timely melodies, as if they are sincerely advising us, saying: "Time is no more, the present is different again, each should be diligent and work hard!"

A bright mirror, sometimes full and sometimes waning, hangs high in the sky, making us feel that all things in the universe are exceptionally clear and bright. The golden osmanthus and the five-colored chrysanthemums by the bamboo fence are illuminated by it, becoming particularly beautiful. But these beautiful flowers will soon be attacked by the merciless—wind—frost—rain—snow—causing them to show a very sad appearance!

Recalling the impressions of the past, imagining the future, and experiencing the present, what we hear and see cannot help but move us within!

Alas! The changes of people and society are like the transformation of the climate. How many people can, like the delicate lotus and the cold-resistant pine, bamboo, and plum, under this severe threat and destruction—struggle—fight—still maintain their fearless spirit; keen thinking; unwavering purpose, quietly enduring, vehemently resisting, and striving hard! (Not for compensation)

Page 22

Talking Points

Crying and Laughing 277

— Yong

"Crying" and "laughing" are innate human functions. A child bursts into tears with a cry to heaven when born from the mother's womb. After some time, under gentle comfort, the child breaks into a small smile. This is a very natural thing, and it may seem trivial to talk about it. However, if we expand on this "crying" and "laughing," from child to adult, from adult to old age; from individual to society, from society to the entire human race; then in the journey between crying and laughing, there lies an unknown amount of human tragedies, reunions, joys, sorrows, and bittersweet events.

Whether it is crying or laughing, both have a moving allure. Encountering a child approaching with a smiling face makes us feel that the child is cute. A woman smiling alluringly at us stirs our hearts, causing an indescribable joy. Similarly, seeing a child with a tearful face causes a feeling of unbearable sorrow. Seeing a woman sobbing uncontrollably, we can't help but feel love out of pity.

Many writers like to laugh and cry, and they praise "crying" and "laughing" as beautiful expressions and supreme art. Indeed, nothing in the world is more deeply and acutely touching than the feelings of "crying" and "laughing." Chinese poets and writers have the lament, "Seeing true emotions in a cry." The Japanese literary master Kuson Shiro in his book Suffering's Symbol also sings that laughter is the poetry of humanity, the art of humanity. The Soviet Union, this uniquely meaningful country, also has the government encouraging the nation to laugh by hanging signs. Bernard Shaw's "Back to Methuselah" is now popular everywhere.

Crying is praised, and laughing is even more formally promoted. However, living in today's desolate and tragic world, on the battlefield of life-and-death struggles, there are dry bones, wreckage, "one general's success bought with ten thousand bones" of laughter, and "still dreaming of her spring boudoir" of tears.

However, looking again at this broken and melancholy China, disasters flow horizontally, desolate villages and stores have turned into scorched earth, selling wives and children, even exchanging children for food. What joy is there to laugh about, what thoughts are there to cry about?

What love is there in crying? This is simply not the human world. There is not only no laughter, but there are simply no people crying.

Humorists may laugh out loud, but if they run to those desolate villages and stores, who will laugh with them when facing those ferocious, hungry faces? The poets and writers who praise "Seeing true emotions in a cry" also no longer have that kind of mournful lament to praise... Crying under the gates of the powerful, unable to get a grain of food, and on that ferocious, hungry face, not even tears can flow.

This broken and melancholy China is such a terrible scene, without emotion, without love, only struggle, only cruel exploitation.

Perhaps some people have jumped out of this tragic circle, crying and laughing. But the crying and laughing outside the circle has no real meaning; it is a vain illusion, a reflection of an empty life, and fundamentally speaking, it has no emotion and no love.

Crying and laughing, guided as the poetry of humanity and the art of humanity, must be elevated from the living base of this dark mass of people, restoring social peace, emotion, and love before they can appear.

Chrysanthemums 278

— Jing Jia

Today, I happened to pull down a collection of Chekhov's novels from the bookshelf and found a faded chrysanthemum petal in the book. Memories of the past were stirred up again.

Last year, it was also this time of year, one afternoon. I invited Hua to go to the Zhaofeng Garden to appreciate the autumn scenery. I wore a half-new lined jacket, and Hua added a short blue woolen

Page 23

jacket over her green cheongsam. We brought a novel, wanting to spend this afternoon in the park immersed in the autumn scenery.

When we arrived at the park, it presented us with a unique and interesting scene. The wind carried fallen leaves in a dance; trees that were lush with branches and leaves a month ago were gradually becoming bald like old men. Only the towering evergreen trees provided us with a model of invigorating spirit.

Hua loves flowers. She likes to sit under the flowers and let them embrace her. In the past, I couldn't muster much interest in flowers, but later I was influenced by her, and I also came to love flowers. Because we both love flowers, we unhesitatingly left the towering evergreen trees and searched everywhere for flower clusters.

Although autumn, like spring, is a mild season, the flowers of autumn cannot compare to those of spring. In spring, flowers can be found everywhere, but finding flowers in autumn is a difficult task. We put in a lot of effort searching and finally found a cluster of chrysanthemums in full bloom in a corner, like Columbus discovering the New World. The color was pink, slightly tinged with yellow.

So we happily exchanged glances, each with a satisfied smile, then we spread our handkerchiefs on the ground and sat down side by side.

Hua gently plucked a chrysanthemum, smelled it at her nose, and lightly placed the flower on her apple-colored cheek. I stared at the flower in a daze.

"Lovely chrysanthemum!" Hua said softly.

"Chrysanthemums are not lovely!" I said with a serious face.

"Why?" Hua asked with a slightly嗔怪 tone: "They are very lovely!"

"Because there is something even lovelier than chrysanthemums!" I laughed.

At first, Hua deliberately pursed her lips, pretending to be angry. Later, she laughed too. She loosened her hand, the chrysanthemum straightened up again, and shook off some withered petals, which fell on our hair and clothes.

Hua picked up a bunch of petals, held them in her palm, and swayed them gently, like a loving mother stroking her beloved child.

"Chrysanthemums are always lovely! How brave they are, blooming proudly under this frost!" Hua said, puffing out her chest.

I nodded. Then I laughed and said, "You have some masculine spirit!"

We spent an afternoon like this; in laughter, in the fragrance of flowers.

When it was time to return, we picked up a few petals and tucked them into a book. We hoped that the fragrance of chrysanthemums would last forever.

Now, this petal of chrysanthemum is in my hand again. Part of the fragrance of the chrysanthemum remains, but where is the "something even lovelier than chrysanthemums!"

Chrysanthemum, I hope you will always preserve your fragrance! Chrysanthemum, I hope you will always be so pure and lovely! I want you to often give me sweet memories! But I don't want you to be a knowing symbol of our separation!

The Art of Facial Expression 279

— Shen Min

Mixing in social circles and engaging in business dealings requires a close relationship with facial expressions, and they must be artistic. One's attitude must be lively and respectful. Within respect, there must also be humility, and within humility, there must be solemnity. Within solemnity, there must be some humor, and within humor, there should be some practicality. The eyes should also carry a smile, and within the smile, there should be sincerity. Facial expressions are truly difficult. If your degree of respect is excessive, some people will suspect that you have ulterior motives. Once suspicion arises, no matter what you do, you cannot be trusted, and everything will become awkward. Therefore, within respect, you must also be humble and amiable. If you are too humble, some people will treat you as a good source of funds and a pushover, and things unfavorable to you will often happen. Therefore, within humility, you must also be solemn, because status and bearing are entirely expressed through this solemnity. But if you are too solemn, some people will say that you are a moralist, pedantic, and stubborn, which will make people fear you. Therefore, within solemnity, you must also have some humor, but the humor must be appropriate. If it is all frivolous and absurd, then nothing can be accomplished, so it must also have some practicality. In short, to get along in this society of fickle affections and thin human relationships, one must have an attitude of庄谐, rounded,巧言令色, or it will be impossible to achieve ultimate victory.

There is a saying that calls someone "honest." As long as one is honest, no matter how twisted their heart or how fierce their methods, as long as they are resourceful, well-rounded, and use them appropriately, they can achieve success in everything. With such abilities, one can be considered a truly comprehensive, first-rate sociable person.

As for the facial expressions of high-ranking officials and gentlemen, they present a different scene. They display a stern and fierce expression, and put on an imposing air. Once they have power in their hands, they fear nothing. It seems that this is the only way to express the status of a big shot.

This is not surprising, because the deep-rooted nature of autocracy in our country is too strong. How can we talk about eliminating class concepts, let alone the word "equality"?

Regarding Japan and the US 280

— Ying Dai

Recently, the matter of eight rice shops in Shanghai fraudulently using foreign brand names to import a large quantity of Japanese rice has suddenly escalated again.

China is an agricultural country, vast and rich in resources, known to the world for producing large quantities of agricultural products. Although it imports other industrial products due to scientific backwardness, it should always export rice and wheat. However, the reality is not so. According to recent customs reports, rice and wheat also have considerable imports every year, which truly makes people "utterly perplexed"!

If its own rice is not enough to supply the needs of its people, then logically demand should exceed supply, and rice prices should be high. But recently, rice prices have been low, and there is a widespread panic about "cheap grain hurting farmers," which is even more "incomprehensible"!

Japan is small in area, with limited agricultural production. The average farmer is also suffering from famine and has no food to eat. But this time, Japan has a large amount of rice to transport to China for sale. Can it be that they would rather starve their own people, but they must transport grain abroad? This is another "incomprehensible thing"!

In short, in today's world, everything, perhaps, is those "incomprehensible things"? The bombardments of September 18th and January 28th by unnamed famous painters' calligraphy and paintings of landscapes, Kong Baiyun, were from Huai Ji, who could write poetry and was especially skilled in stone carving.

We do not know how many Chinese people were killed. But before the bloodstains of the victims were dry, the un-victimized were willing to trade with the enemy and order large quantities of foreign rice.

"The hearts of the people are dead!" "Five points of warmth!" have been seen through by foreigners, so they can bomb China with airplanes and cannons as much as they want. After bombing, the Chinese will forget. When the planes are overhead, they think to themselves that they can no longer buy XX goods, but as soon as the planes pass, they forget. As long as they can make money, any business is acceptable.

The wave of "rural bankruptcy"! "Cheap grain hurts farmers"! has shaken the entire China, but the rice merchants in Shanghai are afraid that rice prices are still too high and that farmers have not starved to death yet, so they transport large quantities of Japanese rice to cause rice prices to continue to fall.

Among the 400 million compatriots in China, farmers are in the majority. Now that rice prices are so low, and the countryside is nine out of ten bankrupt, it can be said that the people of China are nineteen out of ten in dire straits.

The only way to maintain the solvency of the countryside is to raise rice prices to a considerable level. But now the rice merchants, who only care about their own private interests, disregard the lives of farmers and promote the sale of Japanese rice as much as possible, causing Chinese rice to fall further. Aren't they trying to put more than 300 million farmers in China in a desperate situation?
